These days, the depth of her artistry is being recognized by critics and fans alike, and she’s not only crafting hits for others, but blossoming into the performing artist she’s always wanted to be. Her first big show was on a global stage, closing the 2016 Olympics in Brazil with Kygo, singing “Carry Me” to fans around the world. To kick off her LIFT cycle, Michaels performed “Worst In Me” in a stripped-down setting in LA, Great performance. 'channelId': 'UC-VRJ-bPoCAAhQ4cQOrX1nw', 'title': 'Chopin Ballade No. 1 in G minor, Op 23', 'description': 'Frédéric Chopin\'s four Ballades are one-movement pieces for solo piano, composed between 1835 and 1842 in various parts of France and Spain. They are some of the most challenging pieces in the standard piano repertoire.\nThe term "ballade" was associated with French poetry until the mid-19th century, when Chopin was among the first to pioneer the ballade as a musical form. The influence for these four Ballades is claimed to be the poet Adam Mickiewicz. The exact inspiration for each individual Ballade, however, is unclear and disputed. It is clear, however, that they are a novel innovation of Chopin\'s, and that the Ballades cannot be placed into another (e.g. the sonata) form. The Ballades have also directly influenced composers such as Franz Liszt and Johannes Brahms who, after Chopin, wrote Ballades of their own.\nBesides the sharing of the title, the four ballades are distinct entities from each other. According to composer and music critic Louis Ehlert, "Each [Ballade] differs entirely from the others, and they have but one thing in common -- their romantic working out and the nobility of their motives." \nThe four ballades are among the most enduring of Chopin\'s compositions, and are frequently heard in concerts today.\n\nThe Ballade No. 1 in G minor Op. 23 is the first of Frédéric Chopin\'s four ballades. It was composed in 1835-36 during the composer\'s early days in Paris and was dedicated to Monsieur le Baron de Stockhausen, Hanoverian ambassador to France, and reportedly inspired by Adam Mickiewicz\'s poem Konrad Wallenrod. Chopin seemed to have been fond of the piece; in a letter to Heinrich Dorn, Robert Schumann commented that, "I received a new Ballade from Chopin. It seems to be a work closest to his genius (although not the most ingenious) and I told him that I like it best of all his compositions. After quite a lengthy silence he replied with emphasis, \'I am happy to hear this since I too like it most and hold it dearest.\'"\nThe piece begins with a brief introduction which is thematically unrelated to the rest of the piece. It ends with a dissonant left hand chord D, G, and E-flat. Though Chopin\'s original manuscript clearly marks an E-flat as the top note, the chord has caused some degree of controversy, and thus, some versions of the work - such as the Klindworth edition - include D, G, D as an ossia. The main section of the ballade is built from two main themes. The brief introduction fades into the first theme, introduced at measure 7. After some elaboration, the second theme is introduced softly at measure 69. This theme is also elaborated on. Both themes then return in different keys, and the first theme finally returns again in the same key, albeit with an altered left hand accompaniment. A thundering chord introduces the coda, marked Presto con fuoco, which ends the piece. As a whole, the piece is structurally complex and not strictly confined to any particular form, but incorporates ideas from mainly the sonata and variation forms.\n\nTechnically, many passages of the ballade require rapid scales, very fast and large chords, octaves, and difficult fingerings.\nA distinguishing feature of the Ballade No. 1 is its time signature. While all the other ballades are written in strict compound duple time, with a 6/8 time signature, this ballade bears deviations from this. The introduction is written in 4/4 time, and the more extensive Presto con fuoco coda is written in 2/2. The rest of the piece is written in 6/4, rather than the 6/8 which characterizes the other ballades.[6]\nThis ballade is one of the more popular Chopin pieces. It is prominently featured in the 2002 Roman Polanski film The Pianist, where an approximately four-minute cut is played by Janusz Olejniczak. It is also played in the 1944 film Gaslight and heard in the 2006 satire Thank You for Smoking. Many noteworthy pianists have performed and recorded the piece, including Vladimir Horowitz, Alfred Cortot, Arthur Rubinstein, Maurizio Pollini, Krystian Zimmerman & Emil Gilels.', 'thumbnails': {'default': {'url': 'https://i.ytimg.com/vi/wgPh3mSYf0M/default.jpg', 'width': 120, 'height': 90}, 'medium': {'url': 'https://i.ytimg.com/vi/wgPh3mSYf0M/mqdefault.jpg', 'width': 320, 'height': 180}, 'high': {'url': 'https://i.ytimg.com/vi/wgPh3mSYf0M/hqdefault.jpg', 'width': 480, 'height': 360}, 'standard': {'url': 'https://i.ytimg.com/vi/wgPh3mSYf0M/sddefault.jpg', 'width': 640, 'height': 480}}, 'channelTitle': 'Draguve', 'playlistId': 'PLkC1ELgs_K3-P-_EnufZ5FiRAuH6vfvyi', 'resourceId': {'kind': 'youtube#video', 'videoId': 'wgPh3mSYf0M'}}}{'kind': 'youtube#playlistItem', 'etag': '"Fznwjl6JEQdo1MGvHOGaz_YanRU/83TrMOpg_SBOXUnwQF7E3gjwGv8"', 'id': 'UExrQzFFTGdzX0szLVAtX0VudWZaNUZpUkF1SDZ2ZnZ5aS44QTY2MEEzNzBFQUJCMUQ2', 'snippet': {'publishedAt': '2020-02-11T09:01:00.000Z', 'channelId': 'UC-VRJ-bPoCAAhQ4cQOrX1nw', 'title': 'Kreisler-Rachmaninov "Liebesleid" (Love`s Sorrow) Karen Kornienko, piano', 'description': 'this music on Spotify https://open.spotify.com/album/4furHrcbLJpaFFhNCscbGO\nhttp://karenkornienko.ru/en/ - web-site of Karen Kornienko\nhttps://www.amazon.com/dp/B07DP3PPDF/ref=dm_ws_tlw_trk8\nФ.Крейслер-С.Рахманинов. De bijbehorende videoclip is te zien via het Nouveau Riche YouTube kanaal.\n\nNa een hete zomer, waarin Mr Polska samen met Nouveau Riche het clubcircuit en verschillende festivals onveilig maakten, is de Pool terug met nieuw werk. \'Hausa Wausa\' is de naam van de eerste single die verschijnt nadat Mr Polska in maart zijn debuutalbum \'Waardevolle Gezelligheid\' uitbracht.\nMr Polska laat op Hausa Wausa horen stiekem een fascinatie te hebben voor zagen. Hij wil feesten, los gaan en vooral "superveel zagen" op de productie van Boaz van de Beatz die zich hier perfect voor leent.\n\nAan State Magazine vertelt Mr. Polska: "Ik had na al die optredens het gevoel dat ik \'Waardevolle Gezelligheid\' niet langer moest oprekken en heb zin om iets nieuws te laten horen. Boaz en ik zijn ook weer zoveel verder. We maken andere muziek, de structuur van nummers zit bijvoorbeeld ook wat anders in elkaar. Het voelde beter om Hausa Wausa uit te brengen. Het is een trap-nummer, met happy hardcore en een gekke bubbling drop. Dat laatste is echt iets nieuws. Ik ken geen raptracks met een drop er in. Op \'Allermooiste Feestje\' hebben we dat geprobeerd en dat is echt dat ding geworden. Het is draaibaar, Boaz kan zich uitleven en het publiek reageert er goed op."\n\nDe videoclip bij het nummer komt van de hand van Walker Pachler die eerder al een veelgeprezen video\'s maakte voor Dope D.O.D. De leden van Nouveau Riche zijn namelijk (soms meerdere malen) genomineerd in bijna elke categorie.
